22/02/23, 8:20â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: def find_exhibits_on_floor(tokens, json_file):
    f_no = None
    exhibits = []

    # Find the floor number in the tokens
    for i, token in enumerate(tokens):
        if token.isdigit() and int(token) > 0:
            # Assume the floor number is the first positive integer found in the input
            f_no = int(token)
            break
    
    # If a floor number was found, get the exhibits on that floor from the JSON file
    if f_no is not None:
        for exhibit in data["exhibits"]:
            if exhibit["floor"] == f_no:
                exhibits.append(exhibit["name"])

    print(exhibits)

28/02/23, 7:57â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: import subprocess

def main():
    while True:
        print("Starting application...")
        process = subprocess.Popen(["python", "your_application.py"])
        process.wait()
        if process.returncode == 0:
            print("Application shut down successfully.")
            break
        else:
            print("Application was shut down unexpectedly. Restarting...")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

04/04/23, 12:42â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: @app.before_request
def block_attacker():
    """
    Block IP addresses after 3 failed access attempts in the last 5 minutes
    """
    ip = request.remote_addr
    user = session.get("username")
    
    # If the user is not logged in, allow the request
    if 'username' not in session:
        return
    
    # Initialize user's access attempts count
    if user not in user_access_count:
        user_access_count[user] = 0
    
    # Block the IP if the user has made 3 failed access attempts in the last 5 minutes
    if user_access_count[user] >= 3:
        if ip == user_ips[user]:
            # Block the IP address for the user
            abort(403, 'Access Forbidden')
        else:
            # Reset the access count for the user
            user_access_count[user] = 0
    
    # Store the user's IP address
    user_ips[user] = ip

15/04/23, 10:38â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: @socketio.on('send_message')
def handle_message(data):
    # Get the current contact from the session
    contact = session.get('contact')
    if contact not in session['contacts']:
        return redirect('/')
    
    username = session.get("username")
    try:
        room = session.get('room')
    except KeyError:
        room = f"{username}_{contact}"

    message = data
    content = f"{username}: {message}"
    # Encrypt message using ETE
    encrypted_message = ete.encrypt(content)
    emit(content, room=room)
    session['contacts'][contact]["messages"].append(content)

23/04/23, 10:25â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: import socket
import threading

class Peer:
    def __init__(self, name, ip_address, port):
        self.name = name
        self.ip_address = ip_address
        self.port = port
        self.socket = socket.socket(socket.AF_INET, socket.SOCK_STREAM)
        self.connected_peers = []

    def start(self):
        self.socket.bind((self.ip_address, self.port))
        self.socket.listen()
        while True:
            conn, addr = self.socket.accept()
            threading.Thread(target=self.handle_connection, args=(conn,)).start()

    def handle_connection(self, conn):
        data = conn.recv(1024)
        message = data.decode('utf-8')
        message_parts = message.split(':')
        sender = message_parts[0]
        recipient = message_parts[1]
        message_text = message_parts[2]
        if recipient == self.name:
            print(f'Message received: {message_text}')
        else:
            self.forward_message(message)

    def forward_message(self, message):
        for peer in self.connected_peers:
            if peer != self.name:
                try:
                    s = socket.socket(socket.AF_INET, socket.SOCK_STREAM)
                    s.connect((peer.ip_address, peer.port))
                    s.send(message.encode('utf-8'))
                    s.close()
                    print(f'Message forwarded to {peer.name}')
                except:
                    pass

    def connect_to_peer(self, peer):
        try:
            s = socket.socket(socket.AF_INET, socket.SOCK_STREAM)
            s.connect((peer.ip_address, peer.port))
            s.send(f'{self.name}:{peer.name}:Hello'.encode('utf-8'))
            s.close()
            self.connected_peers.append(peer.name)
            print(f'Connected to {peer.name}')
        except:
            print(f'Unable to connect to {peer.name}')

# Sample usage
a = Peer('A', 'localhost', 5000)
b = Peer('B', 'localhost', 5001)
c = Peer('C', 'localhost', 5002)

a.connect_to_peer(b)
b.connect_to_peer(a)
b.connect_to_peer(c)
c.connect_to_peer(b)

a.start()

23/04/23, 10:34â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: import socket
import threading
from multiprocessing import Value

class Peer:
    def __init__(self, name, ip_address, port):
        self.name = name
        self.ip_address = ip_address
        self.port = port
        self.socket = socket.socket(socket.AF_INET, socket.SOCK_STREAM)
        self.connected_peers = []
        self.lock = threading.Lock()
        self.message_counter = Value('i', 0)

    def start(self):
        self.socket.bind((self.ip_address, self.port))
        self.socket.listen()
        while True:
            conn, addr = self.socket.accept()
            threading.Thread(target=self.handle_connection, args=(conn,)).start()

    def handle_connection(self, conn):
        data = conn.recv(1024)
        message = data.decode('utf-8')
        message_parts = message.split(':')
        sender = message_parts[0]
        recipient = message_parts[1]
        message_text = message_parts[2]
        if recipient == self.name:
            with self.message_counter.get_lock():
                self.message_counter.value += 1
            print(f'Message received: {message_text}')
        else:
            self.forward_message(message)

    def forward_message(self, message):
        for peer in self.connected_peers:
            if peer != self.name:
                try:
                    s = socket.socket(socket.AF_INET, socket.SOCK_STREAM)
                    s.connect((peer.ip_address, peer.port))
                    s.send(message.encode('utf-8'))
                    s.close()
                    with self.message_counter.get_lock():
                        self.message_counter.value += 1
                    print(f'Message forwarded to {peer.name}')
                except:
                    pass

    def connect_to_peer(self, peer):
        try:
            s = socket.socket(socket.AF_INET, socket.SOCK_STREAM)
            s.connect((peer.ip_address, peer.port))
            s.send(f'{self.name}:{peer.name}:Hello'.encode('utf-8'))
            s.close()
            with self.lock:
                self.connected_peers.append(peer.name)
            print(f'Connected to {peer.name}')
        except:
            print(f'Unable to connect to {peer.name}')

    def get_message_count(self):
        with self.message_counter.get_lock():
            return self.message_counter.value

21/06/23, 11:27â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: 1. The host has a system clock that resets to epoch time upon reboot. The decision to self-delete can only be determined by examining the time since last reboot and the time since last contact. The time since last contact need not be kept in non-volatile memory, as it is meaningless without a stable system clock. If the device is connected to an unstable power supply which is frequently interrupted, then implant might never be deleted.
2. The host has a system clock that maintains the time across reboots and may or may not be synchronized to an NTP server. Self-deletion can be determined by comparing the time of last contact (maintained via the last modified time of the configuration file) with the current time. If a system administrator changes the time significantly from when implant was first installed and executed, then this action could cause implant to self-delete.
3. The host has a system clock that resets to epoch time upon reboot, but is synchronized to an NTP server at some point after reboot. The self-delete decision for this possibility is similar to that of scenario 2. During a short period after reboot the system clock is near epoch time, so no determination can be made until the clock is set.
21/06/23, 11:27â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: so i was working on a self delete procedure on the hosts side and these are the problems i ran into
21/06/23, 11:28â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: any suggestions?
21/06/23, 11:30â€¯pm - Mainak Dasgupta: So you want it to self delete based on time spent since last contact?
21/06/23, 11:30â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: yup
21/06/23, 11:33â€¯pm - Mainak Dasgupta: You can maintain a record of the time spent in the registry after every unit time or just before shutdown. Then inject a payload to the startup folder that will extract the time spent value from registry on startup or whatever your clock reset event is...and then add to that value recovered from registry...and then keep updating the registry of the machine. Simple registry persistence script should do it.
21/06/23, 11:33â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: ok
21/06/23, 11:33â€¯pm - Agnij Dutta: will try
21/06/23, 11:34â€¯pm - Mainak Dasgupta: That way, the time since last contact will remain absolute and not relative to system clock reset. The rest is just delete itself when the preset absolute time period is over.
